  /** Converts a <button> to look like an <a> tag. */
  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;
    border: 0;

    cursor: pointer;

  h1, h2, h3, h4 {

    color: var(--chops-link-color);
    text-decoration: none;
    font-weight: var(--chops-link-font-weight);
    font-family: var(--chops-font-family);
  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */
    display: inline-flex;
    align-items: center;
    justify-content: center;
    text-decoration: none;

  }
  a.button:hover, .button:hover {

  }

    display: block;

  }

  textarea, select, input {
    box-sizing: border-box;
    font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for
  * accessibility because styles will not always line up with semantically
  * appropriate heading levels.

          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          flex-grow: 1;

          width: 100%;

          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;

          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;

          box-sizing: border-box;

        }

          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;

          max-width: 1000px;

          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);

          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {

          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Due to an issue with the monorail wizard workflow, this issue was not originally labeled as a security bug and, therefore, this issue did not make it to the security team bug queue for triage. This wizard workflow issue was just discovered today, updating accordingly now. 



<span class="line"><!---->Due to an issue with the monorail wizard workflow, this issue was not originally labeled as a security bug and, therefore, this issue did not make it to the security team bug queue for triage. This wizard workflow issue was just discovered today, updating accordingly now. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Tentatively setting these and others as security bugs for general tracking purposes and to go into actual security triage; however, there is no indication that these series of check failure result in security consequences.

Apologies for the lingo. Indeed, I meant the commit range where this bug was introduced/removed. My working theory is that the CHECK failure is non-deterministic, and this has sent ClusterFuzz on a wild goose chase. We should try to do the bisect (i.e. binary search on revisions/commits) manually, taking into account that we need to repeat the test a ton of times for each revision before we can classify it as a true negative. (Whereas a single crash can proof a true positive.)



<span class="line"><!---->Apologies for the lingo. Indeed, I meant the commit range where this bug was introduced/removed. My working theory is that the CHECK failure is non-deterministic, and this has sent ClusterFuzz on a wild goose chase. We should try to do the bisect (i.e. binary search on revisions/commits) manually, taking into account that we need to repeat the test a ton of times for each revision before we can classify it as a true negative. (Whereas a single crash can proof a true positive.)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We could either use `git bisect` or 



<span class="line"><!---->We could either use `git bisect` or <!----></span>





https://www.chromium.org/developers/bisect-builds-py/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.chromium.org/developers/bisect-builds-py/"><!---->https://www.chromium.org/developers/bisect-builds-py/<!----></a>





 for that.

[editing] Make DeleteInsignificantText() to handle spaces causing line break



<span class="line"><!---->[editing] Make DeleteInsignificantText() to handle spaces causing line break<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This patch changes `CompositeEditCommand::DeleteInsignificantText()`



<span class="line"><!---->This patch changes `CompositeEditCommand::DeleteInsignificantText()`<!----></span>



<br>





not to remove `Text` node causing line break.



<span class="line"><!---->not to remove `Text` node causing line break.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





`Text` node causes line break should be significant because it can be



<span class="line"><!---->`Text` node causes line break should be significant because it can be<!----></span>



<br>





rendered when it doesn't cause line break afer changing something



<span class="line"><!---->rendered when it doesn't cause line break afer changing something<!----></span>



<br>





around it.



<span class="line"><!---->around it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>
